  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7f1e7259-1b59-48a5-8c6a-9f1cdddd2c56'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText8284243135551213968" style="display:none"><div>
  <div>SHE MUST CHOOSE BETWEEN HER PEOPLE AND HER FREEDOM...<br /><br />Xylara is the Daughter of the Warrior King, Xyron. With her father dead and her incompetent half-brother on the throne, the kingdom is in danger of falling to the warring Firelanders. <br /><br />Before she was old enough for a marriage-of-alliance, Xylara was trained as a healer. She can't usurp her brother or negotiate a peace--but she can heal the brave ones injured in battle.<br /><br />But not only her countrymen are wounded, and Xylara's conscience won't let Firelander warriors die when she can do something to save them. She learns their language and their customs and tries to make them as comfortable as possible, despite their prisoner-of-war status.<br /><br />She never expects that these deeds, done in good faith, would lead to the handsome and mysterious Firelander Warlord demanding her in exchange for a cease-fire. Xylara knows must trade the life she has always known for the well-being of her people, and so she becomes...<br /><br /><i>The Warprize</i></div>
</div></span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">We find out that in their culture, it is customary for each warrior to produce at least five children before they are allowed to start their training <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">We find out that in their culture, it is customary for each warrior to produce at least five children before they are allowed to start their training to be warriors. None of them raise their own children. It sounded as though other members of their people called "theas" raised the children. Every warrior Lara meets has the tattoos showing the children they had before, even the women.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_29345620" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/29345620" />
    <a title="new_user" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user"><img alt="new_user" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351189841p2/1365355.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/29345620?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="new_user" class="user" itemprop="url" name="new_user" href="/user/show/1365355-new-user">new_user</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1365355-new-user?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer29345620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8023907792694384960"><i>Warprize</i> disappointed me. I had my first clue a few pages in when I realized the prose I could expect would be basic at best, for a romantic fantasy. <br/><br/>While I liked the premise of <i>Warprize</i> and Vaughan's grasp of relationships and human dynamics, the plot was mild, with little conflict to speak of and thus, little suspense or action or even upset. It's all very ho-hum. <br/><br/>I liked the hero Keir -he was to all appearances strong and charming and everything nice, an admittedly refreshing change from the</span>
  <span id="freeText8023907792694384960" style="display:none"><i>Warprize</i> disappointed me. I had my first clue a few pages in when I realized the prose I could expect would be basic at best, for a romantic fantasy. <br /><br />While I liked the premise of <i>Warprize</i> and Vaughan's grasp of relationships and human dynamics, the plot was mild, with little conflict to speak of and thus, little suspense or action or even upset. It's all very ho-hum. <br /><br />I liked the hero Keir -he was to all appearances strong and charming and everything nice, an admittedly refreshing change from the normal gamut of romance heroes- but we only know him superficially, through the heroine's eyes. For those who don't like <b>first person</b> narratives, <i>Warprize</i> embodies all that form's weaknesses. Readers are treated to a painstaking list of the heroine's every mundanity in a flood of monotony: <blockquote>"I...went into the bathing area to remove the dress carefully. I tried to fold it, but the material slipped and slid, the dress ending up on the floor every time. Tired, frustrated and upset, I finally gave up and left it lay on one of the benches. A tunic and trous were set out for me, and I climbed into them for sleeping. After washing out my undergarments, I washed up quickly. My hair was windblown from the tower and the ride, so I gathered up a comb and returned to the other room to try to deal with the tangled mess."</blockquote>Was her editor unavailable that day? I've heard my GoodReads friends describe first person narratives as journal writing. <i>Warprize</i> is journal writing if the writer were a drone. The heroine lists events, lifelessly recounts her reaction in brief (if that) and repeats indefinitely. There is next to no internal dialogue, so we never know the heroine. Since most of these events revolve around her work in the field as a healer, the account becomes excruciatingly repetitive and descends into unnecessary detail (as above). I can't count the number of times I read about Lara brewing fevers foe, but I'm sure a recipe would sum up the book nicely.<br /><br />I can understand completely when readers question whether <i>Warprize</i> can be called a romance. Since the heroine, or more properly, the disinterested observer, has no feelings, there's no sexual tension or tension of any kind. Nine times out of ten, we see the hero from a distance. He's gone fishing most of the time. Else, we receive only a brief report of his dialogue with a woeful lack of body language, or any insight into Keir's character. <br /><br /><i>Warprize</i> is certainly not like the passionate romances, explicit and non-explicit, to which I'm accustomed. It is more appropriately an account of a foreigner in an army camp or a remote ballad. I've seen romances with too much inner dialogue where the heroine stews and wrings her hand endlessly. This is the other end of the spectrum entirely. <b>Two-thirds through the book I finally realized, nothing is happening.</b> It's essentially about the heroine learning about her new people and caring for them. A travelogue, in short. <br /><br />I would recommend this book for someone wanting a calm, mild, relaxed romance with no moral questions, darkness or turbulent emotion. Perhaps on a rainy day. Also, for those wondering, this is PG, maybe 13 for some "kissing" and a vague sex scene. I'm sure this is someone's cuppa. At least the ending was nice.<br /><br />Just a note: there is no middle-eastern culture. Someone mentioned such a label on the book in another review. Just a clarification. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8023907792694384960" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6335924272463392339"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*I Do Like This One*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br/><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 18.11.2020</u>
</b><br/>I adore the beginning of this series. It's a great way to start a book, and to introduce characters personalities. While the book is long and filled with information, it is quite enjoyable. Though I have to be honest and say that I did skim a lot, I still like the book overall. I do wish, however, that Keir showed more... power? He's a damned good leader, but I wanted him to show just how powerful he was, if you know what I mean?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6335924272463392339" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱*I Do Like This One*⋰⋱⋰⋱⋰⋱</b>
</blockquote><br><b>
  <u>Second re-read: 18.11.2020</u>
</b><br>I adore the beginning of this series. It's a great way to start a book, and to introduce characters personalities. While the book is long and filled with information, it is quite enjoyable. Though I have to be honest and say that I did skim a lot, I still like the book overall. I do wish, however, that Keir showed more... power? He's a damned good leader, but I wanted him to show just how powerful he was, if you know what I mean?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>Re-read: 02.04.2017</u>
</b><br>I have <b>no idea why</b> I even started rereading this book. Sure, it's a alright read, but it's not something I'd write home about. <b>Keir, Warlord of the Plains</b> and <b>Xylara “Lara”, Daughter of Xy</b> are cute, separately they are great, the second characters are awesome, the concept and the world is fascinating... however, it's <b>long</b>. And a bit <b>slow</b>. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You tried. That was all you could do. All any of us can do....”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Also, there <b>insta-love</b>, though it is written so one doesn't <i>feel</i> that it is. And frankly, to be honest, I know, deep down, that I started rereading it because of the beginning. I <b>really like the first.. 30%</b> (+-) of the book. So I'm sure I had plans to stop after that, just to have something to do, but then I <b>found myself reading the whole damn thing</b>... damn, I <i>need</i> a life. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Want to know the best part of being a warlord?” came a hoarse whisper.<br>I bit my lip, puzzled by the question.<br>Keir’s mouth curled up slowly into a smile. “I always get what I want.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b><u>Quick basic facts</u>:</b><br><b>Genre</b>: - (Adult) Historical Romance (M/F).<br><b>Series</b>: - Series, Book One.<br><b>Love triangle?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Cheating?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[No. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>HEA?</b> - <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cliffhanger of sorts. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><b>Favorite character?</b> - Warlord Keir.<br><b>Would I read more by this author/or of series?</b> - Unsure.<br><b>Would I recommend this book/series?</b> - Not really, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[it goes downhill from here <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br><b>Will I read this again in the future?</b> - Already did, so who knows...<br><b>Rating</b> - 3 stars<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445268775i/16623124.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b><u>First read review</u>:</b> <br><b>
  <i>Review posted: 26.04.2016</i>
</b> | <b>
  <i>edited: 10.05.2016</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462892806i/19057110.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>I... liked it. Even though it was very long dragged out. I got bored sometimes, but not much, and the characters were lovely. I liked Keir. Very much so. Hell, I liked Keir and Lara as a...couple of sorts, however, I'm not sure if I liked them enough to read even more book about them. Only the future can tell...</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1595454668" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1595454668" />
    <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell"><img alt="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1584062476p2/2190064.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1595454668?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell" href="/user/show/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell">Nenia ✨️ Socially Awkward Trash Panda ✨️ Campbell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11339124-warprize">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=kissing-books">kissing-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=hot-warrior-dudes">hot-warrior-dudes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1595454668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13746700772775771466"><a href='https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>WARPRIZE was a book that I put off reading for a while because I'd hyped it up in my mind so much that I was afraid it wouldn't meet my expectations. But I finally mustered up the courage to read it and much to my surprise and delight, it exceeded my expectations in all ways. This is a slow-burn romance with a light fantasy setting that makes up for the lack of magic with great world-building and a diverse and interesting cast of charact</span>
  <span id="freeText13746700772775771466" style="display:none"><a href="https://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>WARPRIZE was a book that I put off reading for a while because I'd hyped it up in my mind so much that I was afraid it wouldn't meet my expectations. But I finally mustered up the courage to read it and much to my surprise and delight, it exceeded my expectations in all ways. This is a slow-burn romance with a light fantasy setting that makes up for the lack of magic with great world-building and a diverse and interesting cast of characters who are all worth getting to know. I had <i>so much fun </i>reading this fantasy romance.<br><br><br><br>✨ <b>The heroine is a healer</b>. As fun as it can be to read about warrior or assassin heroines who take on their enemies by the sword, it's also sometimes nice to read about people whose strength lies in their intelligence and their kindness. The heroine, Lara, first attracts the attention of the hero because of her steadfast attention to healing the wounded of both camps, including the enemy's. Everyone loves her-- but there's ample reason for it here, which keeps her from coming across as a Mary Sue. Plus, we constantly see her at work and it's such a delightful part of the world-building.<br><br><br><br>✨ <b>The heroine is a compassionate warlord</b>. Picture Khal Drogo, only without the cruel streak. That's Keir, the hero: warlord of a group of people who ride horses on the plains and have just come to an uneasy truce with Lara's people. I could say sooo many great things about Keir, not just that he's hot but also that he's noble and honorable and merciful and kind. Not a pushover by any means, but definitely a man who knows that blood is not always the answer, and that the best way to win the heart of a lady is to treat her with respect and patience. *heart eyes* I stan an honorable man!<br><br><br><br>✨ <b>The court intrigue</b>. Even though the world-building is light, there's still enough tension to keep the pages turning. Lara's half-brother, Xymund, sells her into what he thinks is slavery when he gives her to Keir, and a lot of the book is her slowly coming to trust Keir and his people and realizing that so much of what she believed about them was wrong (and vice-versa). There's also political machinations and assassination attempts, threatening not just Lara's life but also that uneasy peace.<br><br><br><br>✨ <b>The romance</b>. Look, it's slow-burn with some great relationship building with two likable characters who just want to find happiness while also not screwing over their respective people. If you've ever read Grace Draven's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1851213394" rel="nofollow noopener">RADIANCE</a>, you'll know what to expect: it's like a comedy of errors that makes light of the misunderstandings and cultural disconnects of two people from different worlds whose compassion and empathy end up uniting them over their differences.<br><br><br><br>✨ <b>Excellent secondary characters</b>. Whether it was Anna, the temperamental cook; Atira, the female warrior who secretly loves fantasy epics; Simus, the brave and intimidating warrior with the outrageous sense of fashion; Joden, the bard (who reminded me a lot of Jaskier from <i>The Witcher</i>, only with better luck with the ladies), or Warren, Lara's noble guardsman, there were so many people in here who added spice to the story and some genuinely entertaining interactions. <br><br><br><br>Was it cheesy at times? Yes, but that's part of the fun of a fantasy romance, and honestly, this had more depth to it than some of those dudebro fantasy "classics," so even if you don't think you like romance, I'd still recommend it to fantasy readers who enjoy a good character-driven story.<br><br><br><br>4 to 4.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13746700772775771466" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helen 2.0" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helen 2.0" href="/user/show/39575951-helen-2-0">Helen 2.0</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=read-16">read-16</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39575951-helen-2-0?shelf=badass">badass</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1510011522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8431441528192585995">Did anyone else notice that (in the paperback version at least) the spelling of the Warlord's name switched randomly in the middle of the book? For the first couple chapters it was "Kier" and then for the rest of the book it was "Keir". *frowns at editors*<br/><br/>Wow. This book was great. I read it in little bits because I was busy with buddy reads, but I'm glad I didn't give up on it. The writing was lovely, aside from editing oversights *frowns again*, and the world-building... Damn. Too interesting.<br/><br/>L</span>
  <span id="freeText8431441528192585995" style="display:none">Did anyone else notice that (in the paperback version at least) the spelling of the Warlord's name switched randomly in the middle of the book? For the first couple chapters it was "Kier" and then for the rest of the book it was "Keir". *frowns at editors*<br /><br />Wow. This book was great. I read it in little bits because I was busy with buddy reads, but I'm glad I didn't give up on it. The writing was lovely, aside from editing oversights *frowns again*, and the world-building... Damn. Too interesting.<br /><br />Like many mass market romance paperbacks, the conflicts in Warprize were driven by misunderstandings and irrationally evil, jealous assholes. Usually both get on my nerves. However, the misunderstandings were not painfully drawn out and served the plot well; they allowed Lara and Keir to fall in love slowly and against all odds. In this case I could forgive the misunderstandings and overlook Xymund's random and unrealistic evilness.<br />The book was not very fast-paced, but it did introduce a new plot point nearly every chapter to keep me interested.<br /><br />Besides, Lara and Keir are so perfect together! Lara embodies all my goals in life and Keir just kicks ass. Read the book and you'll see what I mean.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1453741036" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1453741036" />
    <a title="Jo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14323468-jo"><img alt="Jo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1434090906p2/14323468.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1453741036?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jo" href="/user/show/14323468-jo">Jo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11339124-warprize">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=mine">mine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14323468-jo?shelf=gr2016">gr2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1453741036" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9861823427423837582"><p>Absolutely fantastic!!!!</p> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It is said that the attraction between warlord and warprize is as the heat of the sun that shines in the height of summer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <p>I love fantasy, but b/c I’m such a romance addict I tend to read more romance than fantasy. It’s rare to find a fantasy book with a sufficient amount of romance, and this book was an absolute treasure ;-) </p> <p>Lara is the daughter of a Warrior King, but for her there’s nothing more important than being a healer. Whether it’s friend or foe, </p></span>
  <span id="freeText9861823427423837582" style="display:none"><p>Absolutely fantastic!!!!</p> <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It is said that the attraction between warlord and warprize is as the heat of the sun that shines in the height of summer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <p>I love fantasy, but b/c I’m such a romance addict I tend to read more romance than fantasy. It’s rare to find a fantasy book with a sufficient amount of romance, and this book was an absolute treasure ;-) </p> <p>Lara is the daughter of a Warrior King, but for her there’s nothing more important than being a healer. Whether it’s friend or foe, anyone who needs medical help she is determined to assist. Her half-brother who is the King is currently at war with the Warlord Keir, and doesn’t like that she is treating the wounded captives.</p> <p>But then Keir wants Lara as the warprize in order to seize the war between him and her kingdom. And because her brother has always hated her, he relished the idea of giving Lara as a slave to Keir. Lara is such a selfless person and so strong willed, that she would do anything to keep her kingdom safe, and so agrees to become the warprize.</p> <p>I utterly enjoyed the plot and world-building of this story. Keir and his warriors are from the Plains and has a different culture and way of speaking. During the time that Lara cared for the wounded warriors she learned their language, but their customs are still very foreign to her, so there were a few of misunderstanding because of this. I loved the fact that being a warprize meant two very different things in the 2 cultures, and I must say I loved Keir’s way more. I also very much enjoyed the character building, and there were many of Keir’s warriors that I just adored.</p> <p>The warriors had no one to treat the wounded back at their camp, and Lara stepped right up to do what she was born to do. I really loved Gils, the little boy, who decided to become her apprentice.</p> <p>Of course the danger is not over now that a truce has been reached, and there are those who would love nothing more than killing Keir and Lara. And it’s up to Keir and his warriors to protect their precious warprize.</p> <blockquote>
  <i>“Want to know the best part of being a warlord?' came a hoarse whisper.<br />I bit my lip, puzzled by the question.<br />Keir’s mouth curled up slowly into a smile. 'I always get what I want.”</i>
</blockquote> <p>Keir was fantastic. Fearsome and a true warrior, he was one very sexy Warlord. I wouldn’t mind being his warprize ;-) I loved that as soon as he found out that Lara’s people only got intimate after they were bonded, he respected this and went about seducing her and winning her trust.</p> <p>I loved the romance in this book. The chemistry between Keir and Lara was intense, but it was slow building, and fit the story perfectly.</p> <p>A really wonderful romantasy (fantasy + romance), and one I would highly recommend.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="9861823427423837582" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_782301915" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/782301915" />
    <a title="Lover of Romance" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance"><img alt="Lover of Romance" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1458253423p2/3709091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/782301915?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lover of Romance" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lover of Romance" href="/user/show/3709091-lover-of-romance">Lover of Romance</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-historical-romance">genre-historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=top-favorites">top-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=favorites-shelf">favorites-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-science-fiction">genre-science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3709091-lover-of-romance?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer782301915" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9358802315979952293">Warpize is the first book in the series, and books 1-3 could actually be one big book, since there are no breaks between books, it just starts off from where the previous book left off. Now for quite some time I kept putting these books off, but I finally decided I needed to try it. Now after reading this book I bought books 2 and 3!!! You go into this book, expecting it to be a average historical themed bodice ripper style of book...well nope it wasn't. Now there are some bodice rippers I love,</span>
  <span id="freeText9358802315979952293" style="display:none">Warpize is the first book in the series, and books 1-3 could actually be one big book, since there are no breaks between books, it just starts off from where the previous book left off. Now for quite some time I kept putting these books off, but I finally decided I needed to try it. Now after reading this book I bought books 2 and 3!!! You go into this book, expecting it to be a average historical themed bodice ripper style of book...well nope it wasn't. Now there are some bodice rippers I love, but I have to say that I LOVE LOVED LOVEDDD this book and what a world that this author has created for us. In Warprize the heroine, Lara, is a healer, and she is a princess, and her step brother is the king. They are at war, with the firelanders. She will aid anyone in need, it doesn't matter if they are friend or foe. So she has been visiting the prisoners to help them in their injuries, one night she heals a man that she learns is a high ranking officer to the firelanders, and she protects him, knowing her brother will have him killed. Then in the marketplace she meets a stranger, a man that makes her burn and she feels a connection she has never felt before. This man, is the warlord, who is demanding that she become his warprize. In Lara's mind, that means she will become his slave. Its either she submits to him or her people will be slaughtered. So she does the right thing, and becomes the Warprize. From the first few days, she starts to realize that this Warlord isn't the typical one, he isn't violent or abusive or raping her. He treats her with respect, and lets her heal others, and roam the camp. Lara still fears him, but when she learns what the "Warprize" really means for him and his culture, Lara will be swept away in a world of magic, desire, and love. The Warprize was such a fantastic read, and I would put it up with my favorites list by far. I am so glad I bought this book, because I plan on reading it again in the near future, I just couldn't get enough of this couple. This story had me in tears and laughing the next moment, Lara is a heroine I came to adore, and what strength she had, and she learns to fight for what she wants most. I was really impressed with this author, what a storyteller she is!! A world that she creates that any fan of C.L. Wilson, MUST READ THIS ONE!!! You will have no regrets!! A story of a tender love, enriching characters, and a plot that thickens with each page!! A STORY TO CAPTIVE YOU FROM THE FIRST PAGE!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9358802315979952293" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78591656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78591656" />
    <a title="Gail Carriger" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2277045-gail-carriger"><img alt="Gail Carriger" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476925453p2/2277045.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78591656?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gail Carriger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gail Carriger" href="/user/show/2277045-gail-carriger">Gail Carriger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2277045-gail-carriger?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78591656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1798057589761316267">This is a culture conflict comfort read for me. I just love the juxtaposition of Keir's pastoral nomadic tribes and Xylara's settled quazi-medieval world. The romance is sweet and poignant but equally balanced against wonderful alt-history fantasy worldbuilding. Side characters are excellent two, and there's solid LBGTQ representation (especially as the series progresses).<br/><br/>I love that there are flaws in culture and knowledge in both cultures, as well as strengths. Xylara must balance the two. I a</span>
  <span id="freeText1798057589761316267" style="display:none">This is a culture conflict comfort read for me. I just love the juxtaposition of Keir's pastoral nomadic tribes and Xylara's settled quazi-medieval world. The romance is sweet and poignant but equally balanced against wonderful alt-history fantasy worldbuilding. Side characters are excellent two, and there's solid LBGTQ representation (especially as the series progresses).<br /><br />I love that there are flaws in culture and knowledge in both cultures, as well as strengths. Xylara must balance the two. I also really enjoy a healer main character. This book never serves me wrong.</span>

<div id="review_1207728934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1207728934" />
    <a title="Jen Davis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis"><img alt="Jen Davis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548427639p2/4669344.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1207728934?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen Davis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen Davis" href="/user/show/4669344-jen-davis">Jen Davis</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1207728934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16633331411204780867">I loved this book. If you enjoy fantasy romance –even a little– I would recommend it without hesitation.<br/><br/>This is a story about people. By that I mean, it’s not an epic fantasy. It’s not about complicated politics or really nuanced worldbuilding. It’s about Lara, a wonderfully drawn healer, and her journey of sacrifice, empathy, and evolution. It’s about her Warlord hero, her friends, and her new community –all created with depth and care; all rich with real personality and designed with an impact</span>
  <span id="freeText16633331411204780867" style="display:none">I loved this book. If you enjoy fantasy romance –even a little– I would recommend it without hesitation.<br /><br />This is a story about people. By that I mean, it’s not an epic fantasy. It’s not about complicated politics or really nuanced worldbuilding. It’s about Lara, a wonderfully drawn healer, and her journey of sacrifice, empathy, and evolution. It’s about her Warlord hero, her friends, and her new community –all created with depth and care; all rich with real personality and designed with an impact on her journey. And it’s about how she falls in love in a way that swept me off my feet and made me believe and cheer and swoon in equal measure.<br /><br />If that doesn’t convince you to give it a try, I don’t know what will.<br /><br />Let me tell you a little about the story. Lara is a healer of her people. She is also a royal princess, half sister to a jealous king who is at war. She takes her calling very seriously, even giving aid to her injured enemies. But when it’s time for peace, her life is turned upside down as she is given to the enroaching Warlord as his Warprize, a station her brother describes as a whore and a slave. She accepts her lot, however, putting her people first, hoping to assure their safety.<br /><br />Lara is quickly immersed in the camp of her new Warlord and must adapt quickly. The romance between her and Keir is very slow in forming, both physically and emotionally, which is part of what makes it so good. Instead of mucking it all up with an insta-love, we see Lara learn her Warlord and his people. Not only do we get to know Keir, but Marcus, Joden, Simus, and so many others. They weave such a rich tapestry of the Plains people –and allow us to see Lara’s true character as she interacts with them all.<br /><br />This book is all from the heroine’s POV, so we don’t get inside Keir’s head. But that was actually kind of pivotal to the way some of the reveals play out.<br /><br />The entire book kept me interested, but when the romance finally came around, it really knocked it out of the park for me. There are some love scenes, which are a bit tamer than I am used to, but work in the context of the story. It all just worked for me. The romance as a whole really engaged me emotionally. I don’t want to spoil too much, but I actually cheered out loud at the ending. I couldn’t have been more satisfied. I loved it.<br /><br />Rating: A</span>
  <a data-text-id="16633331411204780867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3085845624" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3085845624" />
    <a title="Mindy Lou&#39;s Book Review" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review"><img alt="Mindy Lou&#39;s Book Review" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465424458p2/44132489.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/39664779-warprize">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review?shelf=audible-owned">audible-owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review?shelf=hist-romance">hist-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44132489-mindy-lou-s-book-review?shelf=protective-alpha">protective-alpha</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3085845624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9400661582644303475">I found out about Warprize from a book group on Facebook. It was recommended in comparison to Golden Dynasty and Captive of the Horde. I loved both of those books so I had to try this. After reading it, it's defininetly a good comparison while still feeling like it's own book. <br/><br/>The heroine is a strong woman who doesn't frighten easily. She has royal blood but spends her time as a healer. I liked her. This is one of those rare moments where I can say that I have absolutely no complaints where the </span>
  <span id="freeText9400661582644303475" style="display:none">I found out about Warprize from a book group on Facebook. It was recommended in comparison to Golden Dynasty and Captive of the Horde. I loved both of those books so I had to try this. After reading it, it's defininetly a good comparison while still feeling like it's own book. <br /><br />The heroine is a strong woman who doesn't frighten easily. She has royal blood but spends her time as a healer. I liked her. This is one of those rare moments where I can say that I have absolutely no complaints where the heroine is concerned. I think she handled every situation with spirit and grace. <br /><br />The hero is the Warlord. He's a fierce fighter, leader and what you would consider an alpha male. The only thing that felt a bit out of character for him was that he was dominant in everything except the heroine. For being a warlord, you expect him to just take what he wants. He even says he does, but that never really held true when it came to the heroine. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, I still very much enjoyed this book and enjoyed Kier as the hero. I just wish he did a few things differently with the heroine and that would have pushed this into a favorite re-read for me.<br /><br />This doesn't exactly end on a cliffhanger, however you do know there is more to the story. I didn't do my research and I thought this was a standalone book. That's ok for me because I am curious if Keir will be more to character with the heroine considering how this ended. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9400661582644303475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2674461131" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5816699125028641389"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><b>Overall Opinion: </b> I'm super disappointed if I'm being completely honest. This started out and I was really into it, staying up way too late reading one more chapter, thinking "yes! another <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12458287.The_Golden_Dynasty__Fantasyland___2_' title='The Golden Dynasty (Fantasyland, #2) by Kristen Ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Golden Dynasty</a> type book"....but then it flopped. I don't have to have sex in books, but I do need a connection. I liked the tension leading up to Lara being with Kier and H's people, but then everying seemed to fizzle out. No connection to the characters and no connection between them. I felt as </span>
  <span id="freeText5816699125028641389" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars</b><br /><br /><b>Overall Opinion: </b> I'm super disappointed if I'm being completely honest. This started out and I was really into it, staying up way too late reading one more chapter, thinking "yes! another <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12458287.The_Golden_Dynasty__Fantasyland___2_" title="The Golden Dynasty (Fantasyland, #2) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Golden Dynasty</a> type book"....but then it flopped. I don't have to have sex in books, but I do need a connection. I liked the tension leading up to Lara being with Kier and H's people, but then everying seemed to fizzle out. No connection to the characters and no connection between them. I felt as though the connections between Lara and some side characters were the exact same as with Kier. I didn't get any warm fuzzy feelings about how they felt about each other and when it was practically fade-to-black in the (should be) steamy scenes -- I was bummed. I won't even get started on that ending either...just to say, overall, I was disappointed 😔<br /><br /><b>Brief Summary of the Storyline: </b> This is Lara and Kier's story. Lara is a master healer that takes care of the enemy soldiers even though her half-brother king doesn't fully agree with it. She is shocked to find that her half-brother has offered her up as a "warprize" to the enemy ruler in exchange for peace between the people, but Lara instantly agrees to help protect the people she loves. She has to learn to navigate her new reality and in the meantime falls for Kier. There are some suspenseful moments, some funny side characters, and some family drama....and they get a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>Point Of View (POV):</b> This focused mainly on Lara in 3rd person narrative.<br /><br /><b>Overall Pace of Story: </b> Good up until the ending (see closure section below). I never skimmed though.<br /><br /><b>Instalove:</b> Never expressed "ilys" but said each other had one another's hearts. Not much talk of love though...<br /><br /><b>H (Hero) rating:</b> 3 stars. Kier. He was alright. I didn't feel like we truly got to know his character though.<br /><br /><b>h (heroine) rating:</b> 3 stars. Lara. She was also alright. I appreciated her strong morals and wanting to help heal anyone, but it did get kind of annoying when she was constantly defending her half-brother.<br /><br /><b>Sadness level: </b>Low, no tissues needed<br /><br /><b>Push/Pull:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The H pushes away at one point. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Heat level:</b> Low. They have some tension at the beginning -- but that's about it!<br /><br /><b>Descriptive sex:</b> Not quite fade-to-black, but close.<br /><br /><b>OW (Other Woman)/OM (Other Man) drama:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Sex scene with OW or OM:</b> No<br /><br /><b>Cheating: </b> No<br /><br /><b>Separation:</b> Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They are separated shortly, but there was no mention or suggestion of other partners during this time.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Possible Triggers: </b>Yes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Loss of parents (off page), arranged relationship (on page), violence/murder (on page), and the h was a virgin while the H was not.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Closure: </b> This had an abrupt ending with not nearly enough closure! I would call it a HFN ending.<br /><br /><b>Safety:</b> This one is probably <u>Safe with exception </u> for most safety gang readers depending on personal preferences.<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have cheating<br />- <b>Does Not</b> have a descriptive sex scene with OW/OM<br />- <b> Does</b> have the H pushing the h away<br />- <b> Does</b> have a separation between the h and H<br />- <b> Does Not</b> have abuse<br />- <b>Does Not </b> have a HEA ending IMO <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_3187888784" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11339124-warprize">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46741025-anna-lost-in-stories-a?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3187888784" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer465835420342536991">I decided to write just one review for these three books in the series, cause they all tell a story of one couple, Lara and Keir :) originally, I rated the first two book 4 stars, but after a few weeks have passed, I decided to give all three of them 3 stars instead… mostly because the more I thought about it, the more I was sure that it was only a mediocre story for me… don’t get me wrong, I found the first book on sale and was in a mood for a fantasy-ish / historical story with some sort of ar</span>
  <span id="freeText465835420342536991" style="display:none">I decided to write just one review for these three books in the series, cause they all tell a story of one couple, Lara and Keir :) originally, I rated the first two book 4 stars, but after a few weeks have passed, I decided to give all three of them 3 stars instead… mostly because the more I thought about it, the more I was sure that it was only a mediocre story for me… don’t get me wrong, I found the first book on sale and was in a mood for a fantasy-ish / historical story with some sort of arranged relationship in it, so I started reading the first installment straight away… and yes, I was invested enough in the story and curious when it will go that I picked up both sequels right after another… and I did enjoy my time while I was reading them, although I wasn’t the biggest fan of some of the decisions the author made within the story, especially in that third book, but still… I finished them for a reason… but even after only a few weeks I have already forgotten most of the details about it… the main couple was interesting, but I still think their romance was underdeveloped… I can appreciate some topics the author tried to tackle when it comes to a relationship between two strong minded people, but it could have been all handled better… I liked quite a few secondary characters a lot, but even though I already know they have their own stories, if we’re being completely honest, I don’t think I will ever come back to this world… it was all too *meh* for me to spend my time reading even more stories set in it, especially since there are so many more that hit me in all my feels that much stronger… if you are interested in picking this series up then I highly encourage you to check out some other reviews of it before making up your mind :)<br /><br />XOXO<br /><br />A</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200451462" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer7111322208011853001">4.5/5.0<br/>There are books we read for suspense, some we read for the beauty of the word, other's to pit our minds against the authors to solve a mystery. Then, there are some that encompass the very reason books exist... the story. That, that has existed since time began, one person imagining worlds and people and love and trials to rise above, then weaving them into a story to entertain and to teach, the kind people used to tell at bedtime to capture the attention then ponder while drifting off. "</span>
  <span id="freeText7111322208011853001" style="display:none">4.5/5.0<br />There are books we read for suspense, some we read for the beauty of the word, other's to pit our minds against the authors to solve a mystery. Then, there are some that encompass the very reason books exist... the story. That, that has existed since time began, one person imagining worlds and people and love and trials to rise above, then weaving them into a story to entertain and to teach, the kind people used to tell at bedtime to capture the attention then ponder while drifting off. "Warprize" is a consummate example. The beauty of the book is simply in the storytelling and Vaughan is it's most gifted sage. <br /><br />Xylara is a princess who chose to become a healer rather than rule. Keir is a Warlord intent on conquest. He wants her for her abilities, she submits to him for her people. Thus the dance between the needs of many vs the desires of a few. Wonderful! Would have been a resounding 5 stars if not for the horrifically abrupt conclusion. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7111322208011853001" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText4679521887018037677" style="display:none">Someone recommended this book on an "If you liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9237.Jacqueline_Carey" title="Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Jacqueline Carey</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/153008.Kushiel_s_Dart__Ph_dre_s_Trilogy___1_" title="Kushiel's Dart (Phèdre's Trilogy, #1) by Jacqueline Carey" rel="nofollow noopener">Kushiel's Dart</a>..." forum. <br /><br />That was probably an ill-advised recommendation.<br /><br />Other than being nothing at all like Kushiel, this book has its fair share of problems. Most of the book revolves around Lara's tedious daily activities, and it gets old pretty quickly: Healing the wounded, picking off willow bark from stools to make medicine, and exchanging meaningless banter with the warriors of the camp were interesting the first time around--not so much after 40 pages.<br /><br />The only pseudo similarity to the Kushiel series is that the main character, Lara, becomes the sex slave tribute to an invading Warlord--and even that is a bit of a stretch. Given the premise, the romance was perplexingly vanilla and behind-doors. (Nothing against clean romance, but if it's going to be clean, why even bother making the main character a sex slave??)<br /><br />At 44%, I've given this book a fair shot, but ugh, <b>1 star</b></span>

<div id="review_2210058740" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2210058740" />
    <a title="Melanie A. ~mostly on hiatus~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52957386-melanie-a-mostly-on-hiatus"><img alt="Melanie A. ~mostly on hiatus~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1456615487p2/52957386.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2210058740?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie A. ~mostly on hiatus~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie A. ~mostly on hiatus~" href="/user/show/52957386-melanie-a-mostly-on-hiatus">Melanie A. ~mostly on hiatus~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52957386-melanie-a-mostly-on-hiatus?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2210058740" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11384945729566052194"><b>Wow! Can Elizabeth Vaughan ever write!</b><br/><br/>Generally, I like the books I read to have a few layers of smut in them. (Shocking, I know!) So imagine my surprise when I found myself COMPLETELY embroiled in a book where not a single salaciously untoward thing happens! Especially when it's about a woman who's given as tribute to an invading barbarian Warlord. Somehow the author kept it classy, and I should have been disappointed! I should have been outraged! I should have dumped this book back at the libr</span>
  <span id="freeText11384945729566052194" style="display:none"><b>Wow! Can Elizabeth Vaughan ever write!</b><br /><br />Generally, I like the books I read to have a few layers of smut in them. (Shocking, I know!) So imagine my surprise when I found myself COMPLETELY embroiled in a book where not a single salaciously untoward thing happens! Especially when it's about a woman who's given as tribute to an invading barbarian Warlord. Somehow the author kept it classy, and I should have been disappointed! I should have been outraged! I should have dumped this book back at the library with a scowl!<br /><br />But NO! <i>Warprize</i> was awesome! Keir, our Warlord, was a serious bad-ass, but Lara held her own against him; they were wonderfully intense together. Plus, there were some great secondary characters that kept the plot moving along at a brisk pace. I wasn't bored for a single moment. <br /><br />I thought the author did such a fantastic job of reconciling the dark possibilities inherent to a story like this with what actually happened. It was brilliantly done.<br /><br />Best of all, this is a series!!!! If only I could afford to read the sequels..... Since my library only carries the first book, I may just return it with a scowl on my face after all. :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11384945729566052194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1735377257" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735377257" />
    <a title="Minni Mouse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49776720-minni-mouse"><img alt="Minni Mouse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1533535986p2/49776720.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1735377257?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Minni Mouse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Minni Mouse" href="/user/show/49776720-minni-mouse">Minni Mouse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=adult-romance">adult-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=arranged-marriage">arranged-marriage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=cannot-put-down">cannot-put-down</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=pleasantly-surprised">pleasantly-surprised</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=what-the-warlords">what-the-warlords</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=adult-fantasy">adult-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=book-chemistry">book-chemistry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49776720-minni-mouse?shelf=kidnapping">kidnapping</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1735377257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18345272255994599544">I <b>adore</b> stories about falling in love after arranged marriages. This book had the sweet tenderness from <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698409552?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Radiance</a>
</i> (just with a stronger plot apart from the romance), an intelligent healer like Claire from <i><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_' title='Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Outlander</a>,</i> and similar action and story elements as <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735299731?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Golden Dynasty</a>
</i> (but without the tastleless gore and explicit sex). <br/><br/>In short, <i>Warprize</i> was a darling and entertaining story about a brave young woman in the middle of two medieval feuding kingdoms. No prophecies, no magic, no fey fol</span>
  <span id="freeText18345272255994599544" style="display:none">I <b>adore</b> stories about falling in love after arranged marriages. This book had the sweet tenderness from <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1698409552?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiance</a>
</i> (just with a stronger plot apart from the romance), an intelligent healer like Claire from <i><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10964.Outlander__Outlander___1_" title="Outlander (Outlander, #1) by Diana Gabaldon" rel="nofollow noopener">Outlander</a>,</i> and similar action and story elements as <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1735299731?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Golden Dynasty</a>
</i> (but without the tastleless gore and explicit sex). <br /><br />In short, <i>Warprize</i> was a darling and entertaining story about a brave young woman in the middle of two medieval feuding kingdoms. No prophecies, no magic, no fey folk, no bodice-rippers. Just like Goldilocks likes it: juuuusst right.<br /><br /><b>THE GOOD</b><br />1) Xylara. She's not a warrior princess. She's not spunky or rebellious. She's not out-of-this-world beautiful. She's not a political statement and she doesn't have magical powers. Lara is just the daughter of the former king, half-sister to the current king, and an intelligently gifted healer. This means that much of why we like Lara is due to her level-headedness and her passion for healing others. After heroines with magic powers, preternatural assassin skills, or glowing vaginas, it's refreshing to meet a female main character who's noticed for her calm intelligence. <br /><br />2) The set-up. We don't meet Keir until after 20% into the novel, which means for almost the first quarter of the book we are merely seeing her in her natural element. She defies Xymund's orders to leave the POWs alone not because she's making a political statement but rather because her duty to heal and care for others supersedes all of that other mumbo jumbo. We quickly see how her guards and even her enemy patients recognize and quickly respect that quality in her.<br /><br />3) Xylara the Warprize and Keir the Warlord. What a sweet, sweet couple. There are just enough flirty, mildly sensual moments to remind us this <i>is</i> an arranged marriage initiated by Keir, after all, but the rest of their interactions were about bridging each others' cultures and personalities. By the time they get together, it was the perfect moment in context and the most innocently sweet "sex" scene I've read. How refreshing is it when sex is explored from an emotional point of view versus merely physical! <br /><br />4) Supporting characters. Simus and Joden and Marcus were fantastic. More Simus, please!<br /><br /><b>THE BAD</b><br />1) Once again, I find myself searching for that elusive story that has both the right romantic elements <i>and</i> a killer action plot. This book started off fabulously with a tone that remined me of Kestrel and Arin from <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1466960378?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The Winner's Curse.</a>
</i> When I read about Xylara in the beginning doing her own thing and ushering out the POWs to safety and ducking Keir I thought, "All right, all right, I like where this is going!"<br /><br />Well, we didn't quite get there with the political and action intrigue like I wanted...but oh, well. Not that kind of story. <br /><br />2) The ending. Oh, come on. Would it really kill these fantasy authors to end their story with an epic climax filled with sword fights and castle raids and last-stand speeches? <br /><br /><b>THE VERDICT</b><br />Would I recommend this? Absolutely! If you're a fan of arranged marriage stories like I am -- especially with plot elements like a medieval setting, culture shock, and sweet romances -- then you should definitely give this a try. <br /><br />We get drama, medium character development, angsty feels, assassination attempts, and people we distrust. Oh, and a PG-rated adult fantasy book. How often does <i>that</i> happen, eh?</span>
  <a data-text-id="18345272255994599544" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_38774406" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38774406" />
    <a title="Holly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1671402-holly"><img alt="Holly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1296879358p2/1671402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38774406?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly" href="/user/show/1671402-holly">Holly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1671402-holly?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38774406" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2978561878831592386">With an incompetent king on the throne, the kingdom of Xyian is in danger of falling to the Firelanders who swarm outside the city's gates. Thrust into a war that she can do nothing to prevent, Master Healer Xylara, sister to the king, does what she can to prevent the suffering of the men on both sides of the war. Heedless to her brother's demands that she stop treating the enemy, Xylara continues visiting the prisoners, doing the best she can to ease their conditions, and in doing so, brings he</span>
  <span id="freeText2978561878831592386" style="display:none">With an incompetent king on the throne, the kingdom of Xyian is in danger of falling to the Firelanders who swarm outside the city's gates. Thrust into a war that she can do nothing to prevent, Master Healer Xylara, sister to the king, does what she can to prevent the suffering of the men on both sides of the war. Heedless to her brother's demands that she stop treating the enemy, Xylara continues visiting the prisoners, doing the best she can to ease their conditions, and in doing so, brings herself to the attention of the great Warlord himself. If Xyian wishes peace, he demands tribute in the form of Xylara. Proclaimed the Warprize and hailed by the Firelanders, she's told by her spineless brother that she will be nothing but a slave, brought to the Warlord for his pleasure. With a heavy heart, she allows herself to be carried off to the enemy camp, fearful of the future. With miscommunication heavy between them and an enemy intent on destroying the tenuous peace between their two lands, Lara and the Warlord hardly have time to explore the budding desire between them, but explore it they must. For the peace and prosperity of two nations rests on the off chance that the Warlord can claim Lara's heart. <br /><br />This was such a fabulously interesting romantic fantasy done entirely in Lara's POV. I thought this was different and a nice change of pace from what I normally read. While there was a nice romantic element in this story, most of this book is about the cultural gaps between the Xyians and Firelanders and if they will ever be able to bridge them. The antagonist of this story was a little pathetic and it was obvious it was him, but I didn't care. I was mostly interested in the incredible worldbuilding. My absolute favorite part were the "pattern dances" that go on during the middle part of the book. They are intricately choreographed dances that were beautifully described. That part of the story just came to life for me and I enjoyed it immensely. There was alot of humorous little bits running throughout this story, least of which, everyone ignoring Lara's continued pleas that someone call her by her name, instead of constantly referring to her as the Warprize. My only drawback was that I wished this story had more romance in it, a few more one on one interactions between Keir and Lara, but there are two more books in this series so hopefully I can get more from those. <br /><br />Keir, known as the Warlord, was a magnificent male specimen. Your typical rough, tough and brawny warrior who lays claim to his Warprize. He constantly tried to be thoughtful and respectful and was almost too good to be true with his understanding and courteous treatment of Lara. While he doubtlessly wished he could spend his days lounging in naked splendor with his Warprize, he did have a war camp to run and a country to reorganize so that unfortunately left Lara free to roam about the camp. She might be unsure of her place within the hierarchy of the camp but she knows she's a great Healer so she quickly finds her niche. <br /><br />There was a great bunch of characters that Elizabeth Vaughan created and I can't wait to continue indulging in their stories. This wasn't an overly graphic war story, no descriptive battle scenes, nor was the sex overly explicit. The fantastical elements in this story aren't over the top either. There wasn't a huge need to suspend reality. A lot of times I forgot this was a fantasy and thought I was reading a medieval romance. I highly recommend this story and can't wait to read more.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2978561878831592386" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

It had everything I love. An arranged marriage, violence and fighting, treachery, great secondary characters. It just had it all. I was glued to each page. I walked around looking like a zombie for the past 2 days because I stayed up so late reading. </a><br/><br/>I loved Lara. She was stro</span>

  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488904701ra/22166956.gif" alt=" photo thanx_zpsmy2ldov9.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This book was fan-freaking-tastic. I am forever taking your book recommendations after this.<br><br>Ok now, in case you missed it from the beginning paragraph, this book blew my mind. It had everything I love. An arranged marriage, violence and fighting, treachery, great secondary characters. It just had it all. I was glued to each page. I walked around looking like a zombie for the past 2 days because I stayed up so late reading. Was it worth it?<br><a href="http://s1076.photobucket.com/user/kazy7117/media/hell_zpsj6yw9zea.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

She's got my stamp of approval. <br>Now Keir.<br><a href="http://s1076.photobucket.com/user/kazy7117/media/fanning_zpswb3lvcxz.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

Everytime they were together, I had the dumbest looking grin on my face. <br><br>So many of the other characters wormed their way into my heart. Simus, Joden, Atira, Anna the Cook, Heath, too many to name. They were great in both humor and personality. Even the characters I hated were such interesting additions to the story. In particular, I loathed Xymund, Lara's half brother. He was a complete and utter a**hole. He wasn't fit to lead ants, let alone a kingdom, and it killed him that everyone knew it.<br><a href="http://s1076.photobucket.com/user/kazy7117/media/Angry%20Gifs/7275019_zpsui0gedhv.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

From the times when she and Keir finally got to be alone in his tent (wiggling eyebrows), to the times where everything was in chaos between the two nations. Absolutely great story.<br><a href="http://s1076.photobucket.com/user/kazy7117/media/Excited%20Gifs/10590608_zpsryapwoye.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
